<td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%">
<div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini">
<ul>
<li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Homicide" title="Template:Homicide"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li>
<li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Homicide" title="Template talk:Homicide"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li>

</ul>
</div>
</td>

<p>A <b>serial killer</b> is a person who typically <a href="/wiki/Murder" title="Murder">murders</a> three or more people,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Most_common_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-Most_common-1">[1]</a></sup> usually in service of <a href="/wiki/Abnormal_psychology" title="Abnormal psychology">abnormal psychological</a> gratification, with the murders taking place over more than a month and including a significant break (a "cooling off period") between them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Most_common_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-Most_common-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurkhalter_Chmelir20031_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurkhalter_Chmelir20031-2">[2]</a></sup> Different authorities apply different criteria when designating serial killers;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hough_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hough-3">[3]</a></sup> while most set a threshold of three murders,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Most_common_1-2"><a href="#cite_note-Most_common-1">[1]</a></sup> others extend it to four or lessen it to two.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hough_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-Hough-3">[3]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Federal_Bureau_of_Investigation" title="Federal Bureau of Investigation">Federal Bureau of Investigation</a> (FBI), for example, defines serial killing as "a series of two or more murders, committed as separate events, usually, but not always, by one offender acting alone".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurkhalter_Chmelir20031_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurkhalter_Chmelir20031-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMorton20054.2C_9_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMorton20054.2C_9-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>Although psychological gratification is the usual <a href="/wiki/Motive_(law)" title="Motive (law)">motive</a> for serial killing, and most serial killings involve sexual contact with the victim,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGeberth1995.3F_.22The_base_population_was_387_serial_murderers.2C_who_killed_.28under_various_motivations.29.2C_three_or_more_persons_over_a_period_of_time_with_cooling-off_periods_between_the_events._The_author_identified_232_male_serial_murderers_who_violated_their_victims_sexually.22_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGeberth1995.3F_.22The_base_population_was_387_serial_murderers.2C_who_killed_.28under_various_motivations.29.2C_three_or_more_persons_over_a_period_of_time_with_cooling-off_periods_between_the_events._The_author_identified_232_male_serial_murderers_who_violated_their_victims_sexually.22-5">[5]</a></sup> the FBI states that the motives of serial killers can include anger, thrillseeking, financial gain, and <a href="/wiki/Attention_seeking" title="Attention seeking">attention seeking</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMorton20054.2C_9_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMorton20054.2C_9-4">[4]</a></sup> The murders may be attempted or completed in a similar fashion, and the victims may have something in common: age group, appearance, gender, or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Race_(human_classification)" title="Race (human classification)">race</a>, for example.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tick_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tick-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p>Serial killing is not the same as <a href="/wiki/Mass_murder" title="Mass murder">mass murdering</a> (killing numerous people in a given incident); nor is it <a href="/wiki/Spree_killer" title="Spree killer">spree killing</a> (in which murders are committed in two or more locations, in a short time). However, cases of extended bouts of sequential killings over periods of weeks or months with no apparent "cooling off period" or "return to normalcy" have caused some experts to suggest a hybrid category of "spree-serial killer".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-.3DVronsky_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-.3DVronsky-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Serial_killer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The English term and concept of "serial killer" are commonly attributed to former <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/FBI" title="FBI">FBI</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Special_agent_(United_States)" title="Special agent (United States)">Special agent</a> <a href="/wiki/Robert_Ressler" title="Robert Ressler">Robert Ressler</a> in 1974, <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERessler199329_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERessler199329-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchechter20035_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchechter20035-9">[9]</a></sup> and author <a href="/wiki/Ann_Rule" title="Ann Rule">Ann Rule</a> postulates in her book, <i>Kiss Me, Kill Me</i> (2004), that the English-language credit for coining the term <i>serial killer</i> goes to <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Police_Department" title="Los Angeles Police Department">LAPD</a> detective <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Pierce_Brooks&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Pierce Brooks (page does not exist)">Pierce Brooks</a>, who created the <a href="/wiki/Violent_Criminal_Apprehension_Program" title="Violent Criminal Apprehension Program">ViCAP</a> system in 1985.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>However, there is ample evidence the term was used in Europe and the U.S. earlier. The <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a> term and concept were coined by the influential <a href="/wiki/Ernst_Gennat" title="Ernst Gennat">Ernst Gennat</a>, who described <a href="/wiki/Peter_K%C3%BCrten" title="Peter Kürten">Peter Kürten</a> as a <i>Serienmörder</i> (literally "serial murderer") in his article "Die Düsseldorfer Sexualverbrechen" (1930).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> And, according to the <i>Oxford English Dictionary</i>, the specific term "serial killer" first arose abroad in a 1960s German film article written by <a href="/wiki/Siegfried_Kracauer" title="Siegfried Kracauer">Siegfried Kracauer</a>, about the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German_expressionist" title="German expressionist">German expressionist</a> film <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/M_(1931)" title="M (1931)"><i>M</i></a> (1931), portraying a pedophilic <i>Serienmörder</i>.</p>
<p>in his book <i><a href="/wiki/Serial_Killers:_The_Method_and_Madness_of_Monsters" title="Serial Killers: The Method and Madness of Monsters">Serial Killers: The Method and Madness of Monsters</a></i> (2004), criminal justice historian <a href="/wiki/Peter_Vronsky" title="Peter Vronsky">Peter Vronsky</a> argues that while Ressler might have coined the term "serial homicide" within law, at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bramshill_Police_College" title="Bramshill Police College">Bramshill Police Academy</a> in Britain, the terms "serial murder" and "serial murderer" appear in John Brophy's book <i>The Meaning of Murder</i> (1966).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-.3DVronsky_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-.3DVronsky-7">[7]</a></sup> In his more recent study, Vronsky states that the term "serial killing" first entered into American popular usage when published in <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> in the spring of 1981, to describe Atlanta serial killer <a href="/wiki/Wayne_Williams" title="Wayne Williams">Wayne Williams</a>. Subsequently, throughout the 1980s, the term was used in the pages of <i>The New York Times</i> on 233 occasions, but by the end of the 1990s, in the publication's second decade, the use of the term escalated to 2,514 times in the nation's "newspaper of record".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-.3DVronsky-c_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-.3DVronsky-c-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Characteristics">Characteristics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Serial_killer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Characteristics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="General">General</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Serial_killer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: General">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Some commonly found characteristics of serial killers include the following:</p>
<ul>
<li>They may exhibit varying degrees of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mental_illness" title="Mental illness">mental illness</a> and/or <a href="/wiki/Psychopathy" title="Psychopathy">psychopathy</a>, which may contribute to their homicidal behavior.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fbi.gov_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-fbi.gov-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gap_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-gap-14">[14]</a></sup>
<ul>
<li>For example, someone who is mentally ill may have <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Psychotic" title="Psychotic">psychotic</a> breaks that cause them to believe they are another person or are compelled to murder by other entities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBartol2004145_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBartol2004145-15">[15]</a></sup></li>
<li>Psychopathic behavior that is consistent with traits common to some serial killers include sensation seeking, a lack of <a href="/wiki/Remorse" title="Remorse">remorse</a> or <a href="/wiki/Guilt_(emotion)" title="Guilt (emotion)">guilt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Impulsivity" title="Impulsivity">impulsivity</a>, the need for control, and predatory behavior.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fbi.gov_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-fbi.gov-13">[13]</a></sup> Unlike people with major mental disorders such as <a href="/wiki/Schizophrenia" title="Schizophrenia">schizophrenia</a>, psychopaths can seem normal and often quite <a href="/wiki/Superficial_charm" title="Superficial charm">charming</a>, a state of adaptation that <a href="/wiki/Psychiatrist" title="Psychiatrist">psychiatrist</a> <a href="/wiki/Hervey_M._Cleckley" title="Hervey M. Cleckley">Hervey Cleckley</a> called the "<a href="/wiki/The_Mask_of_Sanity" title="The Mask of Sanity">mask of sanity</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>They were often <a href="/wiki/Child_abuse" title="Child abuse">abused</a>—<a href="/wiki/Psychological_abuse" title="Psychological abuse">emotionally</a>, <a href="/wiki/Physical_abuse" title="Physical abuse">physically</a> and/or <a href="/wiki/Child_sexual_abuse" title="Child sexual abuse">sexually</a>—by a family member.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tick_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-Tick-6">[6]</a></sup></li>
<li>Serial killers may be more likely to engage in <a href="/wiki/Sexual_fetishism" title="Sexual fetishism">fetishism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Partialism" title="Partialism">partialism</a> or <a href="/wiki/Necrophilia" title="Necrophilia">necrophilia</a>, which are <a href="/wiki/Paraphilia" title="Paraphilia">paraphilias</a> that involve a strong tendency to experience the object of erotic interest almost as if it were a physical representation of the symbolized body. Individuals engage in paraphilias which are organized along a continuum; participating in varying levels of fantasy perhaps by focusing on body parts (partialism), symbolic objects which serve as physical extensions of the body (fetishism), or the anatomical physicality of the human body; specifically regarding its inner parts and sexual organs (one example being necrophilia).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup></li>
<li>A disproportionate number exhibit one, two, or all three of the <a href="/wiki/Macdonald_triad" title="Macdonald triad">Macdonald triad</a> of predictors of future violent behavior:
<ul>
<li>Many are fascinated with <a href="/wiki/Pyromania" title="Pyromania">fire setting</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tick_6-2"><a href="#cite_note-Tick-6">[6]</a></sup></li>
<li>They are involved in <a href="/wiki/Sadomasochism" title="Sadomasochism">sadistic</a> activity; especially in children who have not reached sexual maturity, this activity may take the form of <a href="/wiki/Zoosadism" title="Zoosadism">torturing animals</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tick_6-3"><a href="#cite_note-Tick-6">[6]</a></sup></li>
<li>More than 60 percent, or simply a large proportion, <a href="/wiki/Enuresis" title="Enuresis">wet their beds</a> beyond the age of 12.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tick_6-4"><a href="#cite_note-Tick-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> However, recent authorities (see citations in the <a href="/wiki/Enuresis" title="Enuresis">Enuresis</a> section of the Macdonald triad article) question or deny the <a href="/wiki/Statistical_significance" title="Statistical significance">statistical significance</a> of this figure; subsequent research suggests that bed-wetting may not be relevant.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>They were frequently <a href="/wiki/Bullying" title="Bullying">bullied</a> or socially isolated as children or adolescents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tick_6-5"><a href="#cite_note-Tick-6">[6]</a></sup> For example, <a href="/wiki/Henry_Lee_Lucas" title="Henry Lee Lucas">Henry Lee Lucas</a> was ridiculed as a child and later cited the mass rejection by his peers as a cause for his hatred of everyone. <a href="/wiki/Kenneth_Bianchi" title="Kenneth Bianchi">Kenneth Bianchi</a> was teased as a child because he urinated in his pants, suffered twitching, and as a teenager was ignored by his peers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tick_6-6"><a href="#cite_note-Tick-6">[6]</a></sup></li>
<li>Some were involved in petty crimes, such as <a href="/wiki/Fraud" title="Fraud">fraud</a>, <a href="/wiki/Theft" title="Theft">theft</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vandalism" title="Vandalism">vandalism</a>, or similar offenses.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
<li>Often, they have trouble staying employed and tend to work in menial jobs. The FBI, however, states, "Serial murderers often seem normal; have families and/or a steady job."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fbi.gov_13-2"><a href="#cite_note-fbi.gov-13">[13]</a></sup> Other sources state they often come from unstable families.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tick_6-7"><a href="#cite_note-Tick-6">[6]</a></sup></li>
<li>Studies have suggested that serial killers generally have an average or low-average <a href="/wiki/Intelligence_quotient" title="Intelligence quotient">IQ</a>, although they are often described, and perceived, as possessing IQs in the above-average range.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tick_6-8"><a href="#cite_note-Tick-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fbi.gov_13-3"><a href="#cite_note-fbi.gov-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Root_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_Root-20">[20]</a></sup> A sample of 202 IQs of serial killers had a median IQ of 89.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<p>There are exceptions to these criteria, however. For example, <a href="/wiki/Harold_Shipman" title="Harold Shipman">Harold Shipman</a> was a successful professional (a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/General_Practitioner" title="General Practitioner">General Practitioner</a> working for the <a href="/wiki/National_Health_Service" title="National Health Service">NHS</a>). He was considered a pillar of the local community; he even won a professional award for a children's asthma clinic and was interviewed by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Granada_Television" title="Granada Television">Granada Television</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/World_in_Action" title="World in Action">World in Action</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Dennis_Nilsen" title="Dennis Nilsen">Dennis Nilsen</a> was an ex-soldier turned civil servant and <a href="/wiki/Trade_union" title="Trade union">trade unionist</a> who had no previous criminal record when arrested. Neither was known to have exhibited many of the tell-tale signs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Vlado_Taneski" title="Vlado Taneski">Vlado Taneski</a>, a crime reporter, was a career <a href="/wiki/Journalist" title="Journalist">journalist</a> who was caught after a series of articles he wrote gave clues that he had murdered people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russell_Williams_(colonel)" title="Russell Williams (colonel)">Russell Williams</a> was a successful and respected career <a href="/wiki/Royal_Canadian_Air_Force" title="Royal Canadian Air Force">Royal Canadian Air Force</a> Colonel who was convicted of murdering two women, along with fetish burglaries and rapes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ottis_Toole.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="504" data-file-width="340" height="222" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Ottis_Toole.jpg/150px-Ottis_Toole.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Ottis_Toole.jpg/225px-Ottis_Toole.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Ottis_Toole.jpg/300px-Ottis_Toole.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a>

<div class="thumb tright">

<div class="thumbcaption">

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Development">Development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Serial_killer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Many serial killers have faced similar problems in their childhood development. Hickey's Trauma Control Model explains how early childhood trauma can set the child up for <a href="/wiki/Deviance_(sociology)" title="Deviance (sociology)">deviant behavior</a> in adulthood; the child's environment (either their parents or society) is the dominant factor determining whether or not the child's behavior escalates into homicidal activity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHolmes2000107_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHolmes2000107-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<p>Family, or lack thereof, is the most prominent part of a child's development because it is what the child can identify with on a regular basis.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETithecott199738_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETithecott199738-27">[27]</a></sup> "The serial killer is no different from any other individual who is instigated to seek approval from parents, sexual partners, or others."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHale199341_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHale199341-28">[28]</a></sup> This need for approval is what influences children to attempt to develop social relationships with their family and peers, but if they are rejected or neglected, they are unable to do so. This results in the lowering of their self-esteem and helps develop their fantasy world, in which they are in control. According to the Hickey's Trauma Control Model the development of a serial killer is based on an early trauma followed by facilitators (e.g., alcohol, drugs, pornography, or other factors that constitute a facilitator, depending on individual circumstances) and disposition (<a href="/wiki/Attachment_disorder" title="Attachment disorder">an inability to attach being one common factor</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHickey2010107_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHickey2010107-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<p>Family interaction also plays an important role in a child's growth and development. "The quality of their attachments to parents and other members of the family is critical to how these children relate to and value other members of society."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHasselt1999166_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHasselt1999166-30">[30]</a></sup> Wilson and Seaman (1990) conducted a study on incarcerated serial killers, and what they felt was the most influential factor that contributed to their homicidal activity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> Almost all of the serial killers in the study had experienced some sort of environmental problems during their childhood, such as a broken home caused by divorce, or a lack of discipline in the home. It was common for the serial killers to come from a family that had experienced divorce, separation, or the lack of a parent. Furthermore, nearly half of the serial killers had experienced some type of physical or sexual abuse, and even more had experienced emotional neglect.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHasselt1999162_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHasselt1999162-32">[32]</a></sup> When a parent has a <a href="/wiki/Drug" title="Drug">drug</a> or <a href="/wiki/Alcohol" title="Alcohol">alcohol</a> problem, the attention in the household is on the parents rather than the child. This neglect of the child leads to the lowering of their self-esteem and helps develop a fantasy world in which they are in control. Hickey's Trauma Control Model supports how the neglect from parents can facilitate deviant behavior, especially if the child sees substance abuse in action.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHickey2010107_29-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHickey2010107-29">[29]</a></sup> This then leads to <a href="/wiki/Disposition" title="Disposition">disposition</a> (the inability to attach), which can further lead to homicidal behavior, unless the child finds a way to develop substantial relationships and fight the label they receive. If a child receives no support from those around him or her, then he or she is unlikely to recover from the <a href="/wiki/Psychological_trauma" title="Psychological trauma">traumatic</a> event in a positive way. As stated by E. E. Maccoby, "the family has continued to be seen as a major—perhaps <i>the</i> major—arena for socialization".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Chromosomal_make_up">Chromosomal make up</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Serial_killer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Chromosomal make up">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>There have been recent studies looking into the possibility that an abnormality with one's <a href="/wiki/Chromosome" title="Chromosome">chromosomes</a> could be the trigger for serial killers. Two serial killers, <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Joe_Long" title="Bobby Joe Long">Bobby Joe Long</a> and <a href="/wiki/Richard_Speck" title="Richard Speck">Richard Speck</a>, came to attention for reported chromosomal abnormalities. Long had an <a href="/wiki/Klinefelter_syndrome" title="Klinefelter syndrome">extra X chromosome</a>. Speck was erroneously reported to have an <a href="/wiki/XYY_syndrome" title="XYY syndrome">extra Y chromosome</a>; in fact, his <a href="/wiki/Karyotype" title="Karyotype">karyotype</a> was performed twice and was normal each time. Hellen Morrison, an American forensic psychiatrist, said in an interview that while researchers do not have an exact gene identity, the fact that the majority of serial killers are men leads researchers to believe there is "a change associated with the male chromosome make up."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Fantasy">Fantasy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Serial_killer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Fantasy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Children who do not have the <a href="/wiki/Power_(social_and_political)" title="Power (social and political)">power</a> to control the mistreatment they suffer sometimes create a new reality to which they can escape. This new reality becomes their <a href="/wiki/Fantasy_(psychology)" title="Fantasy (psychology)">fantasy</a> that they have total control of and becomes part of their daily existence. In this fantasy world, their emotional development is guided and maintained. According to Garrison (1996), "the child becomes <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sociopathic" title="Sociopathic">sociopathic</a> because the normal development of the concepts of right and wrong and <a href="/wiki/Empathy" title="Empathy">empathy</a> towards others is retarded because the child's emotional and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Social_development" title="Social development">social development</a> occurs within his self-centered fantasies. A person can do no wrong in his own world and the pain of others is of no consequence when the purpose of the fantasy world is to satisfy the needs of one person" (Garrison, 1996). Boundaries between fantasy and reality are lost and fantasies turn to dominance, control, sexual conquest, and violence, eventually leading to murder. Fantasy can lead to the first step in the process of a dissociative state, which, in the words of Stephen Giannangelo, "allows the serial killer to leave the stream of consciousness for what is, to him, a better place".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Giannangelo1996_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-Giannangelo1996-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Criminology" title="Criminology">Criminologist</a> Jose Sanchez reports, "the young criminal you see today is more detached from his victim, more ready to hurt or kill ... The lack of empathy for their victims among young criminals is just one symptom of a problem that afflicts the whole society."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETithecott199738_27-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETithecott199738-27">[27]</a></sup> Lorenzo Carcaterra, author of <i>Gangster</i> (2001), explains how potential criminals are <a href="/wiki/Labeling_theory" title="Labeling theory">labeled by society</a>, which can then lead to their offspring also developing in the same way through the <a href="/wiki/Cycle_of_violence" title="Cycle of violence">cycle of violence</a>. The ability for serial killers to appreciate the mental life of others is severely compromised, presumably leading to their dehumanization of others. This process may be considered an expression of the intersubjectivity associated with a cognitive deficit regarding the capability to make sharp distinctions between other people and inanimate objects. For these individuals, objects can appear to possess animistic or humanistic power while people are perceived as objects.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETithecott199743_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETithecott199743-37">[37]</a></sup> Before he was executed, serial killer <a href="/wiki/Ted_Bundy" title="Ted Bundy">Ted Bundy</a> stated media violence and pornography had stimulated and increased his need to commit homicide, although this statement was made during last-ditch efforts to appeal his death sentence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHasselt1999162_32-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHasselt1999162-32">[32]</a></sup> However, correlation is not causation (a disturbed physiological disposition, psychosis, lack of socialization, or aggressiveness may contribute to both fantasy creation and serial killing without fantasy creation generally contributing to serial killing for instance). There are exceptions to the typical fantasy patterns of serial killers, as in the case of <a href="/wiki/Dennis_Rader" title="Dennis Rader">Dennis Rader</a>, who was a loving family man and the leader of his church.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Organized.2C_disorganized.2C_and_mixed">Organized, disorganized, and mixed</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Serial_killer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Organized, disorganized, and mixed">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ted_Bundy_headshot.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="830" data-file-width="600" height="208" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Ted_Bundy_headshot.jpg/150px-Ted_Bundy_headshot.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Ted_Bundy_headshot.jpg/225px-Ted_Bundy_headshot.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Ted_Bundy_headshot.jpg/300px-Ted_Bundy_headshot.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ted_Bundy_headshot.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Ted_Bundy" title="Ted Bundy">Ted Bundy</a> in custody, Florida, July 1978 (State Archives of Florida)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/FBI" title="FBI">FBI</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Crime_Classification_Manual" title="Crime Classification Manual">Crime Classification Manual</a></i> places serial killers into three categories: <i>organized</i>, <i>disorganized</i>, and <i>mixed</i> (i.e., offenders who exhibit organized and disorganized characteristics).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVronsky200499.E2.80.93100_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVronsky200499.E2.80.93100-38">[38]</a></sup> Some killers descend from being organized into disorganized as their killings continue, as in the case of <a href="/wiki/Decompensation" title="Decompensation">psychological decompensation</a> or overconfidence due to having evaded capture, or vice versa, as when a previously disorganized killer identifies one or more specific aspects of the act of killing as his/her source of gratification and develops a <i>modus operandi</i> structured around those.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Organized serial killers often plan their crimes methodically, usually abducting victims, killing them in one place and disposing of them in another. They often lure the victims with ploys appealing to their sense of sympathy. Others specifically target <a href="/wiki/Prostitution" title="Prostitution">prostitutes</a>, who are likely to go voluntarily with a stranger. These killers maintain a high degree of control over the <a href="/wiki/Crime_scene" title="Crime scene">crime scene</a> and usually have a solid knowledge of <a href="/wiki/Forensic_science" title="Forensic science">forensic science</a> that enables them to cover their tracks, such as burying the body or weighing it down and sinking it in a river. They follow their crimes in the <a href="/wiki/News_media" title="News media">news media</a> carefully and often take pride in their actions, as if it were all a grand project. Often, organized killers have social and other interpersonal skills sufficient to enable them to develop both personal and romantic relationships, friends and lovers and sometimes even attract and maintain a spouse and sustain a family including children. Among serial killers, those of this type are in the event of their capture most likely to be described by acquaintances as kind and unlikely to hurt anyone. Bundy and <a href="/wiki/John_Wayne_Gacy" title="John Wayne Gacy">John Wayne Gacy</a> are examples of organized serial killers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERessler1993113_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERessler1993113-39">[39]</a></sup> In general, the <a href="/wiki/Intelligence_quotient" title="Intelligence quotient">IQs</a> of organized serial killers tend to be near normal range, with a mean of 94.7. Organized nonsocial offenders tend to be on the higher end of the average, with a mean IQ of 99.2.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-radfordfgcudb_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-radfordfgcudb-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<p>Disorganized serial killers are usually far more impulsive, often committing their murders with a random weapon available at the time, and usually do not attempt to hide the body. They are likely to be unemployed, a loner, or both, with very few friends. They often turn out to have a history of mental illness,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Serial_Killers_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-Serial_Killers-41">[41]</a></sup> and their <a href="/wiki/Modus_operandi" title="Modus operandi">modus operandi</a> (M.O.) or lack thereof is often marked by excessive violence and sometimes <a href="/wiki/Necrophilia" title="Necrophilia">necrophilia</a> and/or sexual violence.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Disorganized serial killers have been found to have a slightly lower mean IQ than organized serial killers, at 92.8.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-radfordfgcudb_40-1"><a href="#cite_note-radfordfgcudb-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Medical_professionals">Medical professionals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Serial_killer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Medical professionals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Angel_of_Mercy_(criminology)" title="Angel of Mercy (criminology)">Angel of Mercy (criminology)</a></div>
<p>Some people with a pathological interest in the power of life and death tend to be attracted to medical professions or acquiring such a job.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESitpond2000.5B.5BCategory:Wikipedia_articles_needing_page_number_citations_from_February_2011.5D.5D.3Csup_class.3D.22noprint_Inline-Template_.22_style.3D.22white-space:nowrap.3B.22.3E.5B.3Ci.3E.5B.5BWikipedia:Citing_sources.7C.3Cspan_title.3D.22This_citation_requires_a_reference_to_the_specific_page_or_range_of_pages_in_which_the_material_appears..7F.27.22.60UNIQ--nowiki-00000041-QINU.60.22.27.7F_.28February_2011.29.22.3Epage.C2.A0needed.3C.2Fspan.3E.5D.5D.3C.2Fi.3E.5D.3C.2Fsup.3E_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESitpond2000.5B.5BCategory:Wikipedia_articles_needing_page_number_citations_from_February_2011.5D.5D.3Csup_class.3D.22noprint_Inline-Template_.22_style.3D.22white-space:nowrap.3B.22.3E.5B.3Ci.3E.5B.5BWikipedia:Citing_sources.7C.3Cspan_title.3D.22This_citation_requires_a_reference_to_the_specific_page_or_range_of_pages_in_which_the_material_appears..7F.27.22.60UNIQ--nowiki-00000041-QINU.60.22.27.7F_.28February_2011.29.22.3Epage.C2.A0needed.3C.2Fspan.3E.5D.5D.3C.2Fi.3E.5D.3C.2Fsup.3E-42">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWhittle2000.5B.5BCategory:Wikipedia_articles_needing_page_number_citations_from_February_2011.5D.5D.3Csup_class.3D.22noprint_Inline-Template_.22_style.3D.22white-space:nowrap.3B.22.3E.5B.3Ci.3E.5B.5BWikipedia:Citing_sources.7C.3Cspan_title.3D.22This_citation_requires_a_reference_to_the_specific_page_or_range_of_pages_in_which_the_material_appears..7F.27.22.60UNIQ--nowiki-00000043-QINU.60.22.27.7F_.28February_2011.29.22.3Epage.C2.A0needed.3C.2Fspan.3E.5D.5D.3C.2Fi.3E.5D.3C.2Fsup.3E_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWhittle2000.5B.5BCategory:Wikipedia_articles_needing_page_number_citations_from_February_2011.5D.5D.3Csup_class.3D.22noprint_Inline-Template_.22_style.3D.22white-space:nowrap.3B.22.3E.5B.3Ci.3E.5B.5BWikipedia:Citing_sources.7C.3Cspan_title.3D.22This_citation_requires_a_reference_to_the_specific_page_or_range_of_pages_in_which_the_material_appears..7F.27.22.60UNIQ--nowiki-00000043-QINU.60.22.27.7F_.28February_2011.29.22.3Epage.C2.A0needed.3C.2Fspan.3E.5D.5D.3C.2Fi.3E.5D.3C.2Fsup.3E-43">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELinedecker1990.5B.5BCategory:Wikipedia_articles_needing_page_number_citations_from_February_2011.5D.5D.3Csup_class.3D.22noprint_Inline-Template_.22_style.3D.22white-space:nowrap.3B.22.3E.5B.3Ci.3E.5B.5BWikipedia:Citing_sources.7C.3Cspan_title.3D.22This_citation_requires_a_reference_to_the_specific_page_or_range_of_pages_in_which_the_material_appears..7F.27.22.60UNIQ--nowiki-00000045-QINU.60.22.27.7F_.28February_2011.29.22.3Epage.C2.A0needed.3C.2Fspan.3E.5D.5D.3C.2Fi.3E.5D.3C.2Fsup.3E_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELinedecker1990.5B.5BCategory:Wikipedia_articles_needing_page_number_citations_from_February_2011.5D.5D.3Csup_class.3D.22noprint_Inline-Template_.22_style.3D.22white-space:nowrap.3B.22.3E.5B.3Ci.3E.5B.5BWikipedia:Citing_sources.7C.3Cspan_title.3D.22This_citation_requires_a_reference_to_the_specific_page_or_range_of_pages_in_which_the_material_appears..7F.27.22.60UNIQ--nowiki-00000045-QINU.60.22.27.7F_.28February_2011.29.22.3Epage.C2.A0needed.3C.2Fspan.3E.5D.5D.3C.2Fi.3E.5D.3C.2Fsup.3E-44">[44]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHickey1997142_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHickey1997142-45">[45]</a></sup> These kinds of killers are sometimes referred to as "angels of death"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> or angels of mercy. Medical professionals will kill their patients for money, for a sense of sadistic pleasure, for a belief that they are "easing" the patient's pain, or simply "because they can".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHolmes1998204_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHolmes1998204-47">[47]</a></sup> One such killer was nurse <a href="/wiki/Jane_Toppan" title="Jane Toppan">Jane Toppan</a>, who admitted during her murder trial that she was <a href="/wiki/Lust_murder" title="Lust murder">sexually aroused by death</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Female_Lust_Kill_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-Female_Lust_Kill-48">[48]</a></sup> She would administer a drug mixture to patients she chose as her victims, lie in bed with them and <a href="/wiki/Frotteurism" title="Frotteurism">hold them close to her body</a> as they died.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Female_Lust_Kill_48-1"><a href="#cite_note-Female_Lust_Kill-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
<p>Another medical profession serial killer is <a href="/wiki/Genene_Jones" title="Genene Jones">Genene Jones</a>. It is believed she killed 11 to 46 infants and children while working at Bexar County Medical Center Hospital in San Antonio, Texas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-49">[49]</a></sup> She is currently serving a 99-year sentence for the murder of Chelsea McClellan and the attempted murder of Rolando Santos,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_49-1"><a href="#cite_note-:0-49">[49]</a></sup> and is eligible for parole in 2017 due to a law in Texas at the time of her sentencing to reduce prison overcrowding.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_49-2"><a href="#cite_note-:0-49">[49]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Female">Female</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Serial_killer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Female">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wuornos.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="322" data-file-width="308" height="157" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Wuornos.jpg/150px-Wuornos.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Wuornos.jpg/225px-Wuornos.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Wuornos.jpg/300px-Wuornos.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Wuornos.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Highway prostitute <a href="/wiki/Aileen_Wuornos" title="Aileen Wuornos">Aileen Wuornos</a> killed seven men in Florida between 1989 and 1990</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Female serial killers are rare compared to their male counterparts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ABCnews.go.com_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-ABCnews.go.com-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKelleher199812_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKelleher199812-51">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wilson_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wilson-52">[52]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Frei_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-Frei-53">[53]</a></sup> Sources suggest that female serial killers represented fewer than one in every six known serial murderers in the U.S. between 1800 and 2004 (64 females from a total of 416 known offenders), or that around 15% of U.S. serial killers have been women, with a collective number of victims between 427 and 612.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Farrell_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-Farrell-56">[56]</a></sup> <i>Lethal Ladies'</i> authors, Amanda L. Farrell, Robert D. Keppel, and Victoria B. Titterington state that "the Justice Department indicated 36 female serial killers have been active over the course of the last century."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Farrell_56-1"><a href="#cite_note-Farrell-56">[56]</a></sup> According to <i>The Journal of Forensic Psychiatry &amp; Psychology,</i> there is evidence that 16% of all serial killers are women.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<p>Kelleher and Kelleher (1998) created several categories to describe female serial killers. They used the classifications of <i><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/black_widow" title="wiktionary:black widow">black widow</a></i>, <i>angel of death</i>, <i>sexual predator</i>, <i>revenge</i>, <i>profit or crime</i>, <i>team killer</i>, <i>question of sanity</i>, <i>unexplained</i>, and <i>unsolved</i>. In using these categories, they observed that most women fell into the categories of black widow or team killer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Frei_53-1"><a href="#cite_note-Frei-53">[53]</a></sup> Although motivations for female serial killers can include attention seeking, addiction, or the result of psychopathological behavioral factors,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-concordia1_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-concordia1-58">[58]</a></sup> female serial killers are commonly categorized as murdering men for material gain, usually being emotionally close to their victims,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ABCnews.go.com_50-1"><a href="#cite_note-ABCnews.go.com-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKelleher199812_51-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKelleher199812-51">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wilson_52-1"><a href="#cite_note-Wilson-52">[52]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Frei_53-2"><a href="#cite_note-Frei-53">[53]</a></sup> and generally needing to have a relationship with the victim,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Frei_53-3"><a href="#cite_note-Frei-53">[53]</a></sup> hence the traditional cultural image of the "black widow." In describing murderer <a href="/wiki/Stacey_Castor" title="Stacey Castor">Stacey Castor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Forensic_psychiatry" title="Forensic psychiatry">forensic psychiatrist</a> James Knoll offered a <a href="/wiki/Psychology" title="Psychology">psychological perspective</a> on what defines a "black widow" type. In simple terms, he described it as a woman who kills two or more husbands or lovers for material gain. Though Castor was not officially defined as a serial killer, it is likely that she would have killed again.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ABCnews.go.com_50-2"><a href="#cite_note-ABCnews.go.com-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
<p>One "analysis of 86 female serial killers from the U.S. found that the victims tended to be spouses, children or the elderly".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ABCnews.go.com_50-3"><a href="#cite_note-ABCnews.go.com-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Frei_53-4"><a href="#cite_note-Frei-53">[53]</a></sup> Other studies indicate that since 1975, increasingly strangers are marginally the most preferred victim of female serial killers,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> or that only 26% of female serial killers kill for material gain only.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> Sources state that each killer will have her own proclivities, needs and triggers."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ABCnews.go.com_50-4"><a href="#cite_note-ABCnews.go.com-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wilson_52-2"><a href="#cite_note-Wilson-52">[52]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Frei_53-5"><a href="#cite_note-Frei-53">[53]</a></sup> A review of the published literature on female serial murder stated that "sexual or <a href="/wiki/Sadistic_personality_disorder" title="Sadistic personality disorder">sadistic</a> motives are believed to be extremely rare in female serial murderers, and psychopathic traits and histories of childhood abuse have been consistently reported in these women."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ABCnews.go.com_50-5"><a href="#cite_note-ABCnews.go.com-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Frei_53-6"><a href="#cite_note-Frei-53">[53]</a></sup> A study by Eric W. Hickey (2010) of 64 female serial killers in the U.S. indicated that sexual activity was one of several motives in 10% of the cases, enjoyment in 11% and control in 14%, and that 51% of all U.S. female serial killers murdered at least one woman and 31% murdered at least one child.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> In other cases, women have been involved as an accomplice with a male serial killer as a part of a serial killing team.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ABCnews.go.com_50-6"><a href="#cite_note-ABCnews.go.com-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wilson_52-3"><a href="#cite_note-Wilson-52">[52]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Frei_53-7"><a href="#cite_note-Frei-53">[53]</a></sup> A 2015 study published in <i>The Journal of Forensic Psychiatry &amp; Psychology</i> found that the most common motive for female serial killers was for financial gain and almost 40 percent of them had experienced some sort of mental illness.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Peter_Vronsky" title="Peter Vronsky">Peter Vronsky</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/Female_Serial_Killers" title="Female Serial Killers">Female Serial Killers</a></i> (2007) maintains that female serial killers today often kill for the same reason males do: as a means of expressing rage and control. He suggests that sometimes the theft of the victims' property by the female "black widow" type serial killer appears to be for material gain, but really is akin to a male serial killer's collecting of totems (souvenirs) from the victim as a way of exerting continued control over the victim and reliving it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> By contrast, Hickey states that although popular perception sees "black widow" female serial killers as something of the <a href="/wiki/Victorian_era" title="Victorian era">Victorian</a> past, in his statistical study of female serial killer cases reported in the U.S. since 1826, approximately 75% occurred since 1950.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup></p>
<p>The methods that female serial killers use for murder are frequently covert or low-profile, such as murder by poison (the preferred choice for killing).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ABCnews.go.com_50-7"><a href="#cite_note-ABCnews.go.com-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wilson_52-4"><a href="#cite_note-Wilson-52">[52]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Frei_53-8"><a href="#cite_note-Frei-53">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHolmes1998171_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHolmes1998171-65">[65]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_57-1"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-57">[57]</a></sup> Other methods used by female serial killers include shootings (used by 20%), suffocation (16%), stabbing (11%), and drowning (5%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-concordia1_58-1"><a href="#cite_note-concordia1-58">[58]</a></sup> They commit killings in specific places, such as their home or a health-care facility, or at different locations within the same city or state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVronsky20071.2C_42.E2.80.9343_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVronsky20071.2C_42.E2.80.9343-66">[66]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchechter2003312_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchechter2003312-67">[67]</a></sup> A notable exception to the typical characteristics of female serial killers is <a href="/wiki/Aileen_Wuornos" title="Aileen Wuornos">Aileen Wuornos</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchechter200331_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchechter200331-68">[68]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFox2005117_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFox2005117-69">[69]</a></sup> who killed outdoors instead of at home, used a gun instead of poison, killed strangers instead of friends or family, and killed for personal gratification.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchmid2005231_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchmid2005231-70">[70]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Arrigo_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-Arrigo-71">[71]</a></sup> The most prolific female serial killer in all of history is allegedly <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_B%C3%A1thory" title="Elizabeth Báthory">Elizabeth Báthory</a>. Countess Elizabeth Báthory de Ecsed (Báthory Erzsébet in <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_language" title="Hungarian language">Hungarian</a>, August 7, 1560 – August 21, 1614) was a countess from the renowned <a href="/wiki/B%C3%A1thory_family" title="Báthory family">Báthory family</a>. After her husband's death, she and four collaborators were accused of torturing and killing hundreds of girls and young women, with one witness attributing to them over 600 victims, though the number for which they were convicted was 80. Elizabeth herself was neither tried nor convicted. In 1610, however, she was imprisoned in the Csejte Castle, where she remained bricked in a set of rooms until her death four years later.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVronsky200773_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVronsky200773-72">[72]</a></sup></p>
<p>A 2010 article by Perri and Lichtenwald addressed some of the misperceptions concerning female criminality.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Perri_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-Perri-73">[73]</a></sup> In the article, Perri and Lichtenwald analyze the current research regarding female psychopathy, including case studies of female psychopathic killers featuring <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/M%C3%BCnchausen_syndrome_by_proxy" title="Münchausen syndrome by proxy">Münchausen syndrome by proxy</a>, cesarean section homicide, fraud detection homicide, female kill teams, and a female serial killer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Perri_73-1"><a href="#cite_note-Perri-73">[73]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Juvenile">Juvenile</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Serial_killer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Juvenile">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Juvenile serial killers are uncommon. There are three main categories that juvenile serial killers can fit into: primary, maturing, and secondary killers. There have been studies done to compare and contrast these three groups and to discover similarities and differences between them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> Although these types of serial killers are less common, oftentimes adult serial killers may make their debut at an early age and it can be an opportunity for researchers to study what factors brought about the behavior. According to a dissertation by an Alliant International University-Fresno PhD student, there are several factors that could account for juvenile serial killers. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nature_vs._nurture" title="Nature vs. nurture">Nature vs. nurture</a> is a major focus because it explains how certain environments and family behaviors can directly link to the behavior.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnicity_and_demographics_in_the_U.S.">Ethnicity and demographics in the U.S.</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Serial_killer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Ethnicity and demographics in the U.S.">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The racial demographics regarding serial killers are often subject to debate. In the United States, the majority of reported and investigated serial killers are white males, from a lower-to-middle-class background, usually in their late twenties to early thirties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tick_6-9"><a href="#cite_note-Tick-6">[6]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fbi.gov_13-4"><a href="#cite_note-fbi.gov-13">[13]</a></sup> However, there are African American, Asian, and <a href="/wiki/Hispanic_America" title="Hispanic America">Hispanic</a> (of any race) serial killers as well, and, according to the FBI, based on percentages of the U.S. population, whites are not more likely than other races to be serial killers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fbi.gov_13-5"><a href="#cite_note-fbi.gov-13">[13]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Offender_profiling" title="Offender profiling">Criminal profiler</a> <a href="/wiki/Pat_Brown_(criminal_profiler)" title="Pat Brown (criminal profiler)">Pat Brown</a> says serial killers are usually reported as white because serial killers usually target victims of their own race, and the media typically focuses on "All-American" <a href="/wiki/Missing_white_woman_syndrome" title="Missing white woman syndrome">white and pretty female victims</a> who were the targets of white male offenders; that crimes among <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ethnic_Minorities" title="Ethnic Minorities">minority</a> offenders in urban communities, where crime rates are higher, are under-investigated; and that minority serial killers likely exist at the same ratios as white serial killers for the population. She believes that the myth that serial killers are always white might have become "truth" in some research fields due to the over-reporting of white serial killers in the media.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pat_Brown_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-Pat_Brown-75">[75]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to some sources, the percentage of serial killers who are African American is estimated to be between 13 and 22 percent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> Another study has shown that 16 percent of serial killers are African American, what author Maurice Godwin describes as a "sizeable portion".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> A 2014 Radford/FGCU Serial Killer Database annual statistics report showed that for the decades 1900–2010, the percentage of White serial killers was 52.1% while the percentage of African American serial killers was 40.3%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-radfordfgcudb_40-2"><a href="#cite_note-radfordfgcudb-40">[40]</a></sup> Popular racial stereotypes about the lower intelligence of African-Americans, and the stereotype that serial killers are white males, may explain the media focus on serial killers that are white and the failure to adequately report on those that are black.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Root_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-The_Root-20">[20]</a></sup> Similarly, in a 2005 article Anthony Walsh, professor of criminal justice at Boise State University, argued a review of post-WWII serial killings in America finds that the prevalence of African-American serial killers has typically been drastically underestimated in both professional research literature and the mass media. As a paradigmatic case of this media double-standard, Walsh cites news reporting on white killer <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gary_Heidnik" title="Gary Heidnik">Gary Heidnik</a> and African-American killer <a href="/wiki/Harrison_Graham" title="Harrison Graham">Harrison Graham</a>. Both men were residents of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Philadelphia,_Pennsylvania" title="Philadelphia, Pennsylvania">Philadelphia, Pennsylvania</a>; both imprisoned, tortured and killed several women; and both were arrested only months apart in 1987. "Heidnik received widespread national attention, became the subject of books and television shows, and served as a model for the fictitious Buffalo Bill in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Silence_of_the_Lambs_(novel)" title="The Silence of the Lambs (novel)">Silence of the Lambs</a></i>", writes Walsh, while "Graham received virtually no media attention outside of Philadelphia, despite having been convicted of four more murders than Heidnik".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Motives">Motives</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Serial_killer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Motives">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Motive_(law)" title="Motive (law)">motives</a> of serial killers are generally placed into four categories: <i>visionary</i>, <i>mission-oriented</i>, <i>hedonistic</i> and <i>power or control</i>; however, the motives of any given killer may display considerable overlap among these categories.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHolmes199843.E2.80.9344_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHolmes199843.E2.80.9344-80">[80]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBartol2004284_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBartol2004284-81">[81]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Visionary">Visionary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Serial_killer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Visionary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Visionary serial killers suffer from <a href="/wiki/Psychosis" title="Psychosis">psychotic</a> breaks with reality, sometimes believing they are another person or are compelled to murder by entities such as the <a href="/wiki/Devil" title="Devil">Devil</a> or <a href="/wiki/God" title="God">God</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHolmes199862_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHolmes199862-82">[82]</a></sup> The two most common subgroups are "demon mandated" and "God mandated".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBartol2004145_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBartol2004145-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Herbert_Mullin" title="Herbert Mullin">Herbert Mullin</a> believed the American casualties in the <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_War" title="Vietnam War">Vietnam War</a> were preventing California from experiencing <a href="/wiki/Megathrust_earthquake#The_Big_One" title="Megathrust earthquake">the Big One</a>. As the war wound down, Mullin claimed his father instructed him via <a href="/wiki/Telepathy" title="Telepathy">telepathy</a> to raise the number of "human sacrifices to nature" in order to delay a catastrophic earthquake that would plunge California into the ocean.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERessler1993146_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERessler1993146-83">[83]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/David_Berkowitz" title="David Berkowitz">David Berkowitz</a> ("Son of Sam") is also an example of a visionary killer. He claimed a demon transmitted orders through his neighbor's dog and instructed him to commit murder.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchechter2003291_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchechter2003291-84">[84]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mission-oriented">Mission-oriented</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Serial_killer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Mission-oriented">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Mission-oriented killers typically justify their acts as "ridding the world" of a certain type of person perceived as undesirable, such as <a href="/wiki/Homosexuality" title="Homosexuality">gay or lesbian people</a>, prostitutes, or people of different ethnicity or religion; however, they are generally not psychotic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHolmes199843_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHolmes199843-85">[85]</a></sup> For example, the <a href="/wiki/Zebra_murders" title="Zebra murders">Zebra killers</a> in the San Francisco Bay Area specifically targeted Caucasians.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> Some see themselves as attempting to change society, often to cure a societal ill.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHolmes2002112_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHolmes2002112-87">[87]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hedonistic">Hedonistic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Serial_killer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Hedonistic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>This type of serial killer seeks thrills and derives pleasure from killing, seeing people as expendable means to this goal. <a href="/wiki/Forensic_psychology" title="Forensic psychology">Forensic psychologists</a> have identified three subtypes of the hedonistic killer: "lust", "thrill" and "comfort".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBartol2004146_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBartol2004146-88">[88]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Lust">Lust</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Serial_killer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Lust">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Paul_Durousseau.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="384" data-file-width="312" height="185" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Paul_Durousseau.jpg/150px-Paul_Durousseau.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Paul_Durousseau.jpg/225px-Paul_Durousseau.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Paul_Durousseau.jpg/300px-Paul_Durousseau.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Paul_Durousseau.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Paul_Durousseau" title="Paul Durousseau">Paul Durousseau</a> raped and murdered at least seven young women.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Sex is the primary motive of <a href="/wiki/Lust_murder" title="Lust murder">lust killers</a>, whether or not the victims are dead, and fantasy plays a large role in their killings. Their sexual gratification depends on the amount of torture and <a href="/wiki/Mutilation" title="Mutilation">mutilation</a> they perform on their victims. The sexual serial murderer has a psychological need to have absolute control, dominance, and power over their victims, and the infliction of torture, pain, and ultimately death is used in an attempt to fulfill their need.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> They usually use weapons that require close contact with the victims, such as knives or hands. As lust killers continue with their murders, the time between killings decreases or the required level of stimulation increases, sometimes both.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBartol2004146_88-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBartol2004146-88">[88]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHolmes2001163_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHolmes2001163-90">[90]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDobbert200410.E2.80.9311_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDobbert200410.E2.80.9311-91">[91]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Kenneth_Bianchi" title="Kenneth Bianchi">Kenneth Bianchi</a>, one of the "<a href="/wiki/Hillside_Strangler" title="Hillside Strangler">Hillside Stranglers</a>", murdered women and girls of different ages, races and appearance because his sexual urges required different types of stimulation and increasing intensity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDobbert200410-11_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDobbert200410-11-92">[92]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jeffrey_Dahmer" title="Jeffrey Dahmer">Jeffrey Dahmer</a>, who was repeatedly diagnosed with <a href="/wiki/Borderline_personality_disorder" title="Borderline personality disorder">borderline personality disorder</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-psychological_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-psychological-93">[93]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-:1-94">[94]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RD_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-RD-95">[95]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BG_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-BG-96">[96]</a></sup> searched for his perfect fantasy lover—beautiful, submissive and eternal. As his desire increased, he experimented with drugs, alcohol, and exotic sex. His increasing need for stimulation was demonstrated by the dismemberment of victims, whose heads and genitals he preserved, and by his attempts to create a "living zombie" under his control (by pouring acid into a hole drilled into the victim's skull). Dahmer once said, "Lust played a big part of it. Control and lust. Once it happened the first time, it just seemed like it had control of my life from there on in. The killing was just a means to an end. That was the least satisfactory part. I didn't enjoy doing that. That's why I tried to create living zombies with … acid and the drill." He further elaborated on this, also saying, "I wanted to see if it was possible to make—again, it sounds really gross—uh, zombies, people that would not have a will of their own, but would follow my instructions without resistance. So after that, I started using the drilling technique."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dahmerquotes_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-dahmerquotes-97">[97]</a></sup> He experimented with <a href="/wiki/Cannibalism" title="Cannibalism">cannibalism</a> to "ensure his victims would always be a part of him".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDobbert200411_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDobbert200411-98">[98]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Thrill">Thrill</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Serial_killer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Thrill">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Thrill_killing" title="Thrill killing">Thrill killing</a></div>
<p>The primary motive of a thrill killer is to induce pain or terror in their victims, which provides stimulation and excitement for the killer. They seek the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Adrenaline" title="Adrenaline">adrenaline</a> rush provided by hunting and killing victims. Thrill killers murder only for the kill; usually the attack is not prolonged, and there is no sexual aspect. Usually the victims are strangers, although the killer may have followed them for a period of time. Thrill killers can abstain from killing for long periods of time and become more successful at killing as they refine their <a href="/wiki/Modus_operandi" title="Modus operandi">murder methods</a>. Many attempt to commit the <a href="/wiki/Perfect_crime" title="Perfect crime">perfect crime</a> and believe they will not be caught.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBartol2004146_88-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBartol2004146-88">[88]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoward20044_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoward20044-99">[99]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Robert_Hansen" title="Robert Hansen">Robert Hansen</a> took his victims to a secluded area, where he would let them loose and then hunt and kill them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoward20044_99-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoward20044-99">[99]</a></sup> In one of his letters to <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Bay_Area" title="San Francisco Bay Area">San Francisco Bay Area</a> newspapers, the <a href="/wiki/Zodiac_Killer" title="Zodiac Killer">Zodiac Killer</a> wrote "[killing] gives me the most thrilling experience it is even better than getting your rocks off with a girl".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Graysmith_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-Graysmith-100">[100]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coral_Watts" title="Coral Watts">Coral Watts</a> was described by a surviving victim as "excited and hyper and clappin' and just making noises like he was excited, that this was gonna be fun" during the 1982 attack.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cbs2004_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cbs2004-101">[101]</a></sup> Slashing, stabbing, hanging, drowning, asphyxiating, and strangling were among the ways Watts killed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Comfort_.28profit.29">Comfort (profit)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Serial_killer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Comfort (profit)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Material gain and a comfortable lifestyle are the primary motives of comfort killers. Usually, the victims are family members and close acquaintances. After a murder, a comfort killer will usually wait for a period of time before killing again to allow any suspicions by family or authorities to subside. They often use poison, most notably <a href="/wiki/Arsenic" title="Arsenic">arsenic</a>, to kill their victims. Female serial killers are often comfort killers, although not all comfort killers are female.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBartol2004146_88-3"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBartol2004146-88">[88]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchlesinger2000276_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchlesinger2000276-103">[103]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHolmes200041_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHolmes200041-104">[104]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Dorothea_Puente" title="Dorothea Puente">Dorothea Puente</a> killed her tenants for their <a href="/wiki/Social_Security_(United_States)" title="Social Security (United States)">Social Security</a> checks and buried them in the backyard of her home.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHolmes200044_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHolmes200044-105">[105]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/H._H._Holmes" title="H. H. Holmes">H. H. Holmes</a> killed for insurance and business profits.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHolmes200043_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHolmes200043-106">[106]</a></sup> Professional killers ("<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hitman" title="Hitman">hitmen</a>") may also be considered comfort serial killers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHolmes19987_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHolmes19987-107">[107]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Richard_Kuklinski" title="Richard Kuklinski">Richard Kuklinski</a> charged tens of thousands of dollars for a "hit", earning enough money to support his family in a middle-class lifestyle (Bruno, 1993).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup></p>
<p>Some, like Puente and Holmes, may be involved in and/or have previous convictions for theft, <a href="/wiki/Fraud" title="Fraud">fraud</a>, <a href="/wiki/Debt" title="Debt">non payment of debts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Embezzlement" title="Embezzlement">embezzlement</a> and other crimes of a similar nature. <a href="/wiki/Dorothea_Puente" title="Dorothea Puente">Dorothea Puente</a> was finally arrested on a <a href="/wiki/Parole" title="Parole">parole</a> violation, having been on parole for a previous fraud conviction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2016, the oldest prosecution and conviction of a suspected serial killer (Felix Vail) took place in Louisiana. He was convicted of murder fifty-four years after his wife's death in 1962, which had originally been ruled an accidental drowning, and which occurred only months after Vail took out two life insurance policies on her.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> He is a suspect in the disappearances of two other women – his girlfriend in 1973 and his second wife in 1984.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> The prosecutors were allowed to present evidence of the two disappearances under the <a href="/wiki/Doctrine_of_chances" title="Doctrine of chances">Doctrine of chances</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Power.2Fcontrol">Power/control</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Serial_killer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Power/control">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Illustrated_Police_News_-_Jack_the_Ripper_2.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="337" data-file-width="463" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Illustrated_Police_News_-_Jack_the_Ripper_2.png/220px-Illustrated_Police_News_-_Jack_the_Ripper_2.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Illustrated_Police_News_-_Jack_the_Ripper_2.png/330px-Illustrated_Police_News_-_Jack_the_Ripper_2.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Illustrated_Police_News_-_Jack_the_Ripper_2.png/440px-Illustrated_Police_News_-_Jack_the_Ripper_2.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Illustrated_Police_News_-_Jack_the_Ripper_2.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A policeman discovering the body of prostitute <a href="/wiki/Catherine_Eddowes" title="Catherine Eddowes">Catherine Eddowes</a>, one of <a href="/wiki/Jack_the_Ripper" title="Jack the Ripper">Jack the Ripper</a>'s victims</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The main objective for this type of serial killer is to gain and exert <a href="/wiki/Power_(social_and_political)" title="Power (social and political)">power</a> over their victim. Such killers are sometimes <a href="/wiki/Child_abuse" title="Child abuse">abused as children</a>, leaving them with feelings of powerlessness and inadequacy as adults. Many power- or control-motivated killers <a href="/wiki/Sexual_abuse" title="Sexual abuse">sexually abuse</a> their victims, but they differ from hedonistic killers in that <a href="/wiki/Rape" title="Rape">rape</a> is not motivated by lust (as it would be with a lust murder) but as simply another form of dominating the victim.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> (See article <a href="/wiki/Causes_of_sexual_violence" title="Causes of sexual violence">Causes of sexual violence</a> for the differences regarding anger rape, power rape, and sadistic rape.) <a href="/wiki/Ted_Bundy" title="Ted Bundy">Ted Bundy</a> is an example of a power/control-oriented serial killer. He traveled around the United States seeking women to control.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPeck2000255_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPeck2000255-114">[114]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Serial_killer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Many serial killers claim that a violent culture influenced them to commit murders. During his final interview, <a href="/wiki/Ted_Bundy" title="Ted Bundy">Ted Bundy</a> stated that <a href="/wiki/Hardcore_pornography" title="Hardcore pornography">hardcore pornography</a> was responsible for his actions. Others idolise figures for their deeds or perceived <a href="/wiki/Vigilante" title="Vigilante">vigilante</a> justice, such as <a href="/wiki/Peter_K%C3%BCrten" title="Peter Kürten">Peter Kürten</a>, who idolised <a href="/wiki/Jack_the_Ripper" title="Jack the Ripper">Jack the Ripper</a>, or <a href="/wiki/John_Wayne_Gacy" title="John Wayne Gacy">John Wayne Gacy</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ed_Kemper" title="Ed Kemper">Ed Kemper</a>, who both idolised the actor <a href="/wiki/John_Wayne" title="John Wayne">John Wayne</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tick_6-10"><a href="#cite_note-Tick-6">[6]</a></sup> Many movies, books, and documentaries have been written about serial killers, detailing the lives and crimes that have been committed.
