The movie <i><a class="extiw" href="http://www.imdb.com/title/tt0284929/" title="imdbtitle:0284929">Bundy</a></i>, which was released in 2002, focuses on serial killer <a href="/wiki/Ted_Bundy" title="Ted Bundy">Ted Bundy</a>'s personal life in college, leading up to his execution. Another movie, Dahmer, was released in the same year, and tells the story of <a href="/wiki/Jeffrey_Dahmer" title="Jeffrey Dahmer">Jeffrey Dahmer</a>. Serial killers are also portrayed in fictional media, oftentimes as having substantial intelligence and looking for difficult targets, despite the contradiction with the psychological profile of serial killers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> Killers who have a strong desire for fame or to be renowned for their actions desire media attention as a way of validating and spreading their crimes; fear is also a component here, as some serial killers enjoy causing fear. An example is the <a href="/wiki/Dennis_Rader" title="Dennis Rader">BTK Killer</a>, who sought attention from the press during his murder spree.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Theories">Theories</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Serial_killer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Theories">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Biological_and_sociological">Biological and sociological</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Serial_killer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Biological and sociological">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-globalize" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><img alt="Globe icon." data-file-height="290" data-file-width="350" height="40" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Ambox_globe_content.svg/48px-Ambox_globe_content.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Ambox_globe_content.svg/73px-Ambox_globe_content.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Ambox_globe_content.svg/97px-Ambox_globe_content.svg.png 2x" width="48"/></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span">The examples and perspective in this section <b>deal primarily with the United States and do not represent a <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:WikiProject_Countering_systemic_bias" title="Wikipedia:WikiProject Countering systemic bias">worldwide view</a> of the subject</b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">You may <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Serial_killer&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a>, discuss the issue on the <a href="/wiki/Talk:Serial_killer" title="Talk:Serial killer">talk page</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Article_wizard" title="Wikipedia:Article wizard">create a new article</a>, as appropriate.</span> <small><i>(May 2010)</i></small> <small class="hide-when-compact"><i>(<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Theories for why certain people commit serial murder have been advanced. Some theorists believe the reasons are biological, suggesting serial killers are born, not made, and that their violent behavior is a result of abnormal brain activity. Holmes and Holmes believe that "until a reliable sample can be obtained and tested, there is no scientific statement that can be made concerning the exact role of <a href="/wiki/Biology" title="Biology">biology</a> as a determining factor of a serial killer personality."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHolmes2010b55-56_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHolmes2010b55-56-117">[117]</a></sup> The "Fractured Identity Syndrome" (FIS) is a merging of <a href="/wiki/Charles_Cooley" title="Charles Cooley">Charles Cooley</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Looking_glass_self" title="Looking glass self">looking glass self</a>" and <a href="/wiki/Erving_Goffman" title="Erving Goffman">Erving Goffman</a>'s "virtual" and "actual social identity" theories. The FIS suggests a social event, or series of events, during one's childhood or adolescence results in a fracturing of the personality of the serial killer. The term "fracture" is defined as a small breakage of the personality which is often not visible to the outside world and is only felt by the killer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup></p>
<p>"Social Process Theory" has also been suggested as an explanation for serial murder. Social process theory states that offenders may turn to crime due to peer pressure, family, and friends. Criminal behavior is a process of interaction with social institutions, in which everyone has the potential for criminal behavior.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHickey2010.5B.5BCategory:Wikipedia_articles_needing_page_number_citations_from_February_2011.5D.5D.3Csup_class.3D.22noprint_Inline-Template_.22_style.3D.22white-space:nowrap.3B.22.3E.5B.3Ci.3E.5B.5BWikipedia:Citing_sources.7C.3Cspan_title.3D.22This_citation_requires_a_reference_to_the_specific_page_or_range_of_pages_in_which_the_material_appears..7F.27.22.60UNIQ--nowiki-000000B7-QINU.60.22.27.7F_.28February_2011.29.22.3Epage.C2.A0needed.3C.2Fspan.3E.5D.5D.3C.2Fi.3E.5D.3C.2Fsup.3E_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHickey2010.5B.5BCategory:Wikipedia_articles_needing_page_number_citations_from_February_2011.5D.5D.3Csup_class.3D.22noprint_Inline-Template_.22_style.3D.22white-space:nowrap.3B.22.3E.5B.3Ci.3E.5B.5BWikipedia:Citing_sources.7C.3Cspan_title.3D.22This_citation_requires_a_reference_to_the_specific_page_or_range_of_pages_in_which_the_material_appears..7F.27.22.60UNIQ--nowiki-000000B7-QINU.60.22.27.7F_.28February_2011.29.22.3Epage.C2.A0needed.3C.2Fspan.3E.5D.5D.3C.2Fi.3E.5D.3C.2Fsup.3E-119">[119]</a></sup> A lack of family structure and identity could also be a cause leading to serial murder traits. A child used as a scapegoat will be deprived of their capacity to feel guilt. Displaced anger could result in animal torture, as identified in the <a href="/wiki/Macdonald_triad" title="Macdonald triad">Macdonald triad</a>, and a further lack of basic identity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Serial_killer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Charles_Ng.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="243" data-file-width="214" height="170" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Charles_Ng.jpg/150px-Charles_Ng.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/09/Charles_Ng.jpg 1.5x" width="150"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Charles_Ng.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A dishonorably discharged Marine, <a href="/wiki/Charles_Ng" title="Charles Ng">Charles Ng</a> participated in the kidnapping, sadistic torture, rape and murder of numerous victims</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The "military theory" has been proposed as an explanation for why serial murderers kill, as some serial murderers have served in the military or related fields. According to Castle and Hensley, 7% of the serial killers studied had military experience.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Defronzo_122-0"><a href="#cite_note-Defronzo-122">[122]</a></sup> This figure may be a proportional under-representation when compared to the number of military veterans in a nation's total population. For example, according to the United States census for the year 2000, military veterans comprised 12.7% of the U.S. population;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> in <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a>, it was estimated in 2007 that military veterans comprised 9.1% of the population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> Though by contrast, about 2.5% of the population of <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a> in 2006 consisted of military veterans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup></p>
<p>There are two theories that can be used to study the correlation between serial killing and military training: <i>Applied learning theory</i> states that serial killing can be learned. The military is training for higher kill rates from servicemen while training the soldiers to be desensitized to taking a human life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Castle_127-0"><a href="#cite_note-Castle-127">[127]</a></sup> <i>Social learning theory</i> can be used when soldiers get praised and accommodated for killing. They learn, or believe that they learn, that it is acceptable to kill because they were praised for it in the military. Serial killers want accreditation for the work that they have done.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Exploring_128-0"><a href="#cite_note-Exploring-128">[128]</a></sup></p>
<p>In both military and serial killing, the offender or the soldier may become desensitized to killing as well as compartmentalized; the soldiers do not see enemy personnel as "human" and neither do serial killers see their victims as humans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hamamoto_129-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hamamoto-129">[129]</a></sup> The theories do not imply that military institutions make a deliberate effort to produce serial killers; to the contrary, all military personnel are trained to recognize when, where, and against whom it is appropriate to use deadly force, which starts with the basic <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Laws_of_war" title="Laws of war">Law of Land Warfare</a></i>, taught during the <a href="/wiki/Recruit_training" title="Recruit training">initial training phase</a>, and may include more stringent policies for military personnel in law enforcement or security.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> They are also taught ethics in basic training.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Investigation">Investigation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Serial_killer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Investigation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="FBI:_Issues_and_practices">FBI: Issues and practices</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Serial_killer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: FBI: Issues and practices">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2008, the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Bureau_of_Investigation" title="Federal Bureau of Investigation">Federal Bureau of Investigation</a> (FBI) published a handbook entitled <i>Serial Murder</i> which was the product of a symposium held in 2005 to bring together the many issues surrounding serial murder, including its investigation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_131-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-131">[131]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Identification">Identification</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Serial_killer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Identification">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%C3%81ngel_Maturino_Res%C3%A9ndiz.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="405" data-file-width="276" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/%C3%81ngel_Maturino_Res%C3%A9ndiz.jpg/150px-%C3%81ngel_Maturino_Res%C3%A9ndiz.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/%C3%81ngel_Maturino_Res%C3%A9ndiz.jpg/225px-%C3%81ngel_Maturino_Res%C3%A9ndiz.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/bb/%C3%81ngel_Maturino_Res%C3%A9ndiz.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%C3%81ngel_Maturino_Res%C3%A9ndiz.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/%C3%81ngel_Maturino_Res%C3%A9ndiz" title="Ángel Maturino Reséndiz">Ángel Maturino Reséndiz</a>, who was a <a href="/wiki/FBI_Ten_Most_Wanted_Fugitives" title="FBI Ten Most Wanted Fugitives">FBI Ten Most Wanted Fugitive</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>According to the FBI, identifying one, or multiple, murders as being the work of a serial killer is the first challenge an investigation faces, especially if the victim(s) come from a marginalized or high risk population and is normally linked through forensic or behavioral evidence (FBI 2008).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_131-1"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-131">[131]</a></sup> Should the cases cross multiple jurisdictions, the law enforcement system in the United States is fragmented and thus not configured to detect multiple similar murders across a large geographic area (Egger 1998).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-egger1998_132-0"><a href="#cite_note-egger1998-132">[132]</a></sup> The FBI suggests utilizing databases and increasing interdepartmental communication. Keppel (1989)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-keppel1990_133-0"><a href="#cite_note-keppel1990-133">[133]</a></sup> suggests holding multi-jurisdictional conferences regularly to compare cases giving departments a greater chance to detect linked cases and overcome linkage blindness. One such collaboration, the <i>Radford/FGCU Serial Killer Database Project</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> was proposed at the 2012 <a href="/wiki/International_Association_for_Identification" title="International Association for Identification">FDIAI</a> Annual Conference.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup> Utilizing <a href="/wiki/Radford_University" title="Radford University">Radford</a>'s Serial Killer Database as a starting point, the new collaboration,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> hosted by <a href="/wiki/Florida_Gulf_Coast_University" title="Florida Gulf Coast University">FGCU</a> Justice Studies, has invited and is working in conjunction with other Universities to maintain and expand the scope of the database to also include <a href="/wiki/Spree_killer" title="Spree killer">spree</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mass_murder" title="Mass murder">mass murders</a>. Utilizing over 170 data points, multiple-murderer <a href="/wiki/Methodology" title="Methodology">methodology</a> and <a href="/wiki/Victimology" title="Victimology">victimology</a>; researchers and Law Enforcement Agencies can build <a href="/wiki/Case_study" title="Case study">case studies</a> and <a href="/wiki/Statistics" title="Statistics">statistical</a> profiles to further research the <i>Who, What, Why and How</i> of these types of crimes.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Leadership">Leadership</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Serial_killer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Leadership">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Leadership, or administration, should play a small or virtually non-existent role in the actual investigation past assigning knowledgeable or experienced homicide investigators to lead positions. The administration's role is not to run the investigation but to establish and reaffirm the primary goal of catching the serial killer, as well as provide support for the investigators. The FBI (2008) suggests completing Memorandums of Understanding to facilitate support and commitment of resources from different jurisdictions to an investigation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_131-2"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-131">[131]</a></sup> Egger (1998) takes this one step further and suggests completing mutual aid pacts, which are written agreements to provide support to each other in a time of need, with surrounding jurisdictions. Doing this in advance would save time and resources that could be used on the investigation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-egger1998_132-1"><a href="#cite_note-egger1998-132">[132]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Organization">Organization</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Serial_killer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Organization">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Organization of the structure of an investigation is key to its success, as demonstrated by the investigation of the Green River Killer. Once a serial murder case was established, a task force was created to track down and arrest the offender. Over the course of the investigation, for various reasons, the task force's organization was radically changed and reorganized multiple times – at one point including more than 50 full-time personnel, and at another, only a single investigator. Eventually, what led to the end of the investigation was a conference of 25 detectives organized to share ideas to solve the case.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guillen2007_137-0"><a href="#cite_note-guillen2007-137">[137]</a></sup></p>
<p>The FBI handbook provides a description of how a task force should be organized but offers no additional options on how to structure the investigation. While it appears advantageous to have a full-time staff assigned to a serial murder investigation, it can become prohibitively expensive. For example, the Green River Task Force cost upwards of two million dollars a year,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guillen2007_137-1"><a href="#cite_note-guillen2007-137">[137]</a></sup> and as was witnessed with the Green River Killer investigation, other strategies can prevail where a task force fails.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Albert_deSalvo.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="442" data-file-width="426" height="228" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Albert_deSalvo.jpg/220px-Albert_deSalvo.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Albert_deSalvo.jpg/330px-Albert_deSalvo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/0a/Albert_deSalvo.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Albert_deSalvo.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Albert_De_Salvo" title="Albert De Salvo">Albert De Salvo</a>, who claimed to be the "<a href="/wiki/Boston_Strangler" title="Boston Strangler">Boston Strangler</a>", after being caught in Lynn, Massachusetts in 1967.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>A common strategy, already employed by many departments for other reasons, is the conference, in which departments get together and focus on a specific set of topics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-egger1990_138-0"><a href="#cite_note-egger1990-138">[138]</a></sup> With serial murders, the focus is typically on unsolved cases, with evidence thought to be related to the case at hand.</p>
<p>Similar to a conference is an information clearing-house in which a jurisdiction with a suspected serial murder case collects all of its evidence and actively seeks data which may be related from other jurisdictions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-egger1990_138-1"><a href="#cite_note-egger1990-138">[138]</a></sup> By collecting all of the related information into one place, they provide a central point in which it can be organized and easily accessed by other jurisdictions working toward the goal of arresting an offender and ending the murders.</p>
<p>Already mentioned was the task force,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-egger1990_138-2"><a href="#cite_note-egger1990-138">[138]</a></sup> FBI 2008,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_131-3"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-131">[131]</a></sup> Keppel 1989<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-keppel1990_133-1"><a href="#cite_note-keppel1990-133">[133]</a></sup> which provides for a flexible, organized, framework for jurisdictions depending on the needs of the investigation. Unfortunately due to the need to commit resources (manpower, money, equipment, etc.) for long periods of time it can be an unsustainable option.</p>
<p>In the case of the investigation of Aileen Wournos, the Marion County Sheriff coordinated multiple agencies without any written or formal agreement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-egger1998_132-2"><a href="#cite_note-egger1998-132">[132]</a></sup> While not a specific strategy for a serial murder investigation, this is certainly a best practice in so far as the agencies were able to work easily together toward a common goal.</p>
<p>Finally, once a serial murder investigation has been identified, utilization of an FBI Rapid Response Team can assist both experienced and inexperienced jurisdictions in setting up a task force. This is completed by organizing and delegating jobs, by compiling and analyzing clues, and by establishing communication between the parties involved.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-egger1998_132-3"><a href="#cite_note-egger1998-132">[132]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Resource_augmentation">Resource augmentation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Serial_killer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Resource augmentation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>During the course of a serial murder investigation it may become necessary to call in additional resources; the FBI defines this as Resource Augmentation. Within the structure of a task force the addition of a resource should be thought of as either long term, or short term. If the task force's framework is expanded to include the new resource, then it should be permanent and not removed. For short term needs, such as setting up road blocks or canvassing a neighborhood, additional resources should be called in on a short term basis. The decision of whether resources are needed short or long term should be left to the lead investigator and facilitated by the administration (FBI 2008).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_131-4"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-131">[131]</a></sup> The confusion and counter productiveness created by changing the structure of a task force mid investigation is illustrated by the way the Green River Task Force's staffing and structure was changed multiple times throughout the investigation. This made an already complicated situation more difficult, resulting in the delay or loss of information, which allowed Ridgeway to continue killing (Guillen 2007).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guillen2007_137-2"><a href="#cite_note-guillen2007-137">[137]</a></sup> The FBI model does not take into account that permanently expanding a task force, or investigative structure, may not be possible due to cost or personnel availability. Egger (1998) offers several alternative strategies including; using investigative consultants, or experienced staff to augment an investigative team. Not all departments have investigators experienced in serial murder and by temporarily bringing in consultants, they can educate a department to a level of competence then step out. This would reduce the initially established framework of the investigation team and save the department the cost of retaining the consultants until the conclusion of the investigation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-egger1998_132-4"><a href="#cite_note-egger1998-132">[132]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Communication">Communication</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Serial_killer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Communication">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The FBI handbook (2008)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_131-5"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-131">[131]</a></sup> and Keppel (1989)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-keppel1990_133-2"><a href="#cite_note-keppel1990-133">[133]</a></sup> both stress communication as paramount. The difference is that the FBI handbook (2008)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_131-6"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-131">[131]</a></sup> concentrates primarily on communication within a task force while Keppel (1989)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-keppel1990_133-3"><a href="#cite_note-keppel1990-133">[133]</a></sup> makes getting information out to, and allowing information to be passed back from patrol officers a priority. The FBI handbook (2008)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_131-7"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-131">[131]</a></sup> suggest having daily e-mail or in person briefings for all staff involved in the investigation and providing periodic summary briefings to patrol officer and managers. Looking back on a majority of serial murderer arrests, most are exercised by patrol officers in the course of their every day duties and unrelated to the ongoing serial murder investigation (Egger 1998,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-egger1998_132-5"><a href="#cite_note-egger1998-132">[132]</a></sup> Keppel 1989).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-keppel1990_133-4"><a href="#cite_note-keppel1990-133">[133]</a></sup> Keppel (1989)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-keppel1990_133-5"><a href="#cite_note-keppel1990-133">[133]</a></sup> provides examples of Larry Eyler, who was arrested during a traffic stop for a parking violation, and Ted Bundy, who was arrested during a traffic stop for operating a stolen vehicle. In each case it was uniformed officers, not directly involved in the investigation, who knew what to look for and took the direct action that stopped the killer. By providing up to date (as opposed to periodic) briefings and information to officers on the street the chances of catching a serial killer, or finding solid leads, are increased.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Data_management">Data management</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Serial_killer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Data management">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>A serial murder investigation generates staggering amounts of data, all of which needs to be reviewed and analyzed. A standardized method of documenting and distributing information must be established and investigators must be allowed time to complete reports while investigating leads and at the end of a shift (FBI 2008).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_131-8"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-131">[131]</a></sup> When the mechanism for data management is insufficient, leads are not only lost or buried but the investigation can be hindered and new information can become difficult to obtain or become corrupted. During the Green River Killer investigation, reporters would often find and interview possible victims or witnesses ahead of investigators. The understaffed investigation was unable to keep up the information flow, which prevented them from promptly responding to leads. To make matters worse, investigators believed that the journalists, untrained in interviewing victims or witnesses of crimes, would corrupt the information and result in unreliable leads (Guillen 2007).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guillen2007_137-3"><a href="#cite_note-guillen2007-137">[137]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Serial_killer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_serial_killers_before_1900" title="List of serial killers before 1900">List of serial killers before 1900</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BathoryErzsebet.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="653" height="235" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/BathoryErzsebet.jpg/150px-BathoryErzsebet.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/BathoryErzsebet.jpg/225px-BathoryErzsebet.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/BathoryErzsebet.jpg/300px-BathoryErzsebet.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BathoryErzsebet.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The "Blood Countess", as <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_B%C3%A1thory" title="Elizabeth Báthory">Elizabeth Báthory</a> (1560–1614)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Historical <a href="/wiki/Criminology" title="Criminology">criminologists</a> have suggested that there may have been serial murders throughout history, but specific cases were not adequately recorded. Some sources suggest that legends such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Werewolves" title="Werewolves">werewolves</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vampire" title="Vampire">vampires</a> were inspired by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Medieval" title="Medieval">medieval</a> serial killers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchlesinger20005_139-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchlesinger20005-139">[139]</a></sup> In Africa, there have been periodic outbreaks of murder by <i>Lion</i> and <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Leopard_men" title="Leopard men">Leopard men</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Liu_Pengli" title="Liu Pengli">Liu Pengli</a> of China, cousin of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Han_Dynasty" title="Han Dynasty">Han</a> Emperor <a href="/wiki/Emperor_Jing_of_Han" title="Emperor Jing of Han">Jing</a>, was made Prince of Jidong in the sixth year of the middle period of Jing's reign (144 BC). According to the Chinese historian <a href="/wiki/Sima_Qian" title="Sima Qian">Sima Qian</a>, he would "go out on marauding expeditions with 20 or 30 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slave" title="Slave">slaves</a> or with young men who were in hiding from the law, murdering people and seizing their belongings for sheer sport". Although many of his subjects knew about these murders, it was not until the 29th year of his reign that the son of one of his victims finally sent a report to the Emperor. Eventually, it was discovered that he had murdered at least 100 people. The officials of the court requested that Liu Pengli be executed; however, the emperor could not bear to have his own cousin killed, so Liu Pengli was made a commoner and banished.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEQian2003387_141-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEQian2003387-141">[141]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the 15th century, one of the wealthiest men in Europe and a former companion-in-arms of <a href="/wiki/Joan_of_Arc" title="Joan of Arc">Joan of Arc</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gilles_de_Rais" title="Gilles de Rais">Gilles de Rais</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sexual_assault" title="Sexual assault">sexually assaulted</a> and killed peasant children, mainly boys, whom he had abducted from the surrounding villages and had taken to his castle.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVronsky200445-48_142-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVronsky200445-48-142">[142]</a></sup> It is estimated that his victims numbered between 140 and 800.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVronsky200447_143-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVronsky200447-143">[143]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Hungary" title="Kingdom of Hungary">Hungarian</a> aristocrat <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_B%C3%A1thory" title="Elizabeth Báthory">Elizabeth Báthory</a>, born into one of the wealthiest families in <a href="/wiki/Transylvania" title="Transylvania">Transylvania</a>, allegedly <a href="/wiki/Torture" title="Torture">tortured</a> and killed as many as 650 girls and young women before her arrest in 1610.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVronsky2007b78_144-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVronsky2007b78-144">[144]</a></sup></p>
<p>Members of the <a href="/wiki/Thuggee" title="Thuggee">Thuggee</a> cult in India may have murdered a million people between 1740 and 1840.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Thug_Behram" title="Thug Behram">Thug Behram</a>, a member of the cult, may have murdered as many as 931 victims.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup></p>
<p>In his 1886 book <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Psychopathia_Sexualis_(book)" title="Psychopathia Sexualis (book)">Psychopathia Sexualis</a></i>, psychiatrist <a href="/wiki/Richard_von_Krafft-Ebing" title="Richard von Krafft-Ebing">Richard von Krafft-Ebing</a> noted a case of a serial murderer in the 1870s, a <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">Frenchman</a> named Eusebius Pieydagnelle who had a sexual obsession with blood and confessed to murdering six people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="In_modern_times">In modern times</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Serial_killer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: In modern times">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jack-the-Ripper-The-Nemesis-of-Neglect-Punch-London-Charivari-cartoon-poem-1888-09-29.jpg"><img alt="A phantom brandishing a knife floats through a slum street" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="525" data-file-width="410" height="282" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Jack-the-Ripper-The-Nemesis-of-Neglect-Punch-London-Charivari-cartoon-poem-1888-09-29.jpg/220px-Jack-the-Ripper-The-Nemesis-of-Neglect-Punch-London-Charivari-cartoon-poem-1888-09-29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Jack-the-Ripper-The-Nemesis-of-Neglect-Punch-London-Charivari-cartoon-poem-1888-09-29.jpg/330px-Jack-the-Ripper-The-Nemesis-of-Neglect-Punch-London-Charivari-cartoon-poem-1888-09-29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/8e/Jack-the-Ripper-The-Nemesis-of-Neglect-Punch-London-Charivari-cartoon-poem-1888-09-29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jack-the-Ripper-The-Nemesis-of-Neglect-Punch-London-Charivari-cartoon-poem-1888-09-29.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The 'Nemesis of Neglect': Jack the Ripper depicted as a phantom stalking Whitechapel, and as an embodiment of social neglect, in a <i><a href="/wiki/Punch_(magazine)" title="Punch (magazine)">Punch</a></i> cartoon of 1888.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The unidentified killer <a href="/wiki/Jack_the_Ripper" title="Jack the Ripper">Jack the Ripper</a>, who has been called the first modern serial killer,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Whitechapel_murders" title="Whitechapel murders">killed at least five prostitutes</a>, and possibly more, in <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a> in 1888. He was the subject of a massive manhunt and investigation by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Police" title="Metropolitan Police">Metropolitan Police</a>, during which many modern criminal investigation techniques were pioneered. A large team of policemen conducted house-to-house inquiries, forensic material was collected and suspects were identified and traced.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-canter12_149-0"><a href="#cite_note-canter12-149">[149]</a></sup> Police surgeon <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Bond_(British_physician)" title="Thomas Bond (British physician)">Thomas Bond</a> assembled one of the earliest <a href="/wiki/Offender_profiling" title="Offender profiling">character profiles of the offender</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-canter5_150-0"><a href="#cite_note-canter5-150">[150]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Ripper murders also marked an important watershed in the treatment of crime by journalists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-odnb_151-0"><a href="#cite_note-odnb-151">[151]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-w.26b20_152-0"><a href="#cite_note-w.26b20-152">[152]</a></sup> While not the first serial killer in history, Jack the Ripper's case was the first to create a worldwide media frenzy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-odnb_151-1"><a href="#cite_note-odnb-151">[151]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-w.26b20_152-1"><a href="#cite_note-w.26b20-152">[152]</a></sup> The dramatic murders of financially destitute women in the midst of the wealth of <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>, focused the media's attention on the plight of the urban poor and gained coverage worldwide. Jack the Ripper has also been called the most famous serial killer of all time, and his legend has spawned hundreds of theories on his real identity and multiple works of fiction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Trutv.com.com_153-0"><a href="#cite_note-Trutv.com.com-153">[153]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/H._H._Holmes" title="H. H. Holmes">H. H. Holmes</a> was one of the first documented modern serial killers in America, responsible for the death of at least 27 victims at his hotel in <a href="/wiki/Chicago" title="Chicago">Chicago</a> in the early 1890s. Here as well, the case gained notoriety and wide publicity through <a href="/wiki/William_Randolph_Hearst" title="William Randolph Hearst">William Randolph Hearst</a>'s newspapers. At the same time in <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Vacher" title="Joseph Vacher">Joseph Vacher</a> became known as the "The French Ripper" after killing and mutilating 11 women and children. He was executed in 1898 after confessing to his crimes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TRutv.com.com_154-0"><a href="#cite_note-TRutv.com.com-154">[154]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup></p>
<p>Infamous serial killers of the 20th century include <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Willie_Pickton" title="Willie Pickton">Willie Pickton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Harold_Shipman" title="Harold Shipman">Harold Shipman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Luis_Garavito" title="Luis Garavito">Luis Garavito</a>, <a href="/wiki/Javed_Iqbal_(serial_killer)" title="Javed Iqbal (serial killer)">Javed Iqbal</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anatoly_Onopriyenko" title="Anatoly Onopriyenko">Anatoly Onopriyenko</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dean_Corll" title="Dean Corll">Dean Corll</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Wayne_Gacy" title="John Wayne Gacy">John Wayne Gacy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jeffrey_Dahmer" title="Jeffrey Dahmer">Jeffrey Dahmer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ted_Bundy" title="Ted Bundy">Ted Bundy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peter_Sutcliffe" title="Peter Sutcliffe">Peter Sutcliffe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fritz_Haarmann" title="Fritz Haarmann">Fritz Haarmann</a> and <a href="/wiki/Peter_K%C3%BCrten" title="Peter Kürten">Peter Kürten</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peter_Tobin" title="Peter Tobin">Peter Tobin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Albert_Fish" title="Albert Fish">Albert Fish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ed_Gein" title="Ed Gein">Ed Gein</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fred_West" title="Fred West">Fred West</a>, <a href="/wiki/Richard_Ramirez" title="Richard Ramirez">Richard Ramirez</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Berkowitz" title="David Berkowitz">David Berkowitz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aileen_Wuornos" title="Aileen Wuornos">Aileen Wuornos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rosemary_West" title="Rosemary West">Rosemary West</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Gary_Ridgway" title="Gary Ridgway">Gary Ridgway</a>.</p>
<p>76% of all known serial killers in the 20th century were from the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="In_media_and_popular_culture">In media and popular culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Serial_killer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: In media and popular culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Art">Art</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Serial_killer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Art">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Asesinato_de_Francisco_Guerrero(001).JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="535" data-file-width="700" height="168" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Asesinato_de_Francisco_Guerrero%28001%29.JPG/220px-Asesinato_de_Francisco_Guerrero%28001%29.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Asesinato_de_Francisco_Guerrero%28001%29.JPG/330px-Asesinato_de_Francisco_Guerrero%28001%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Asesinato_de_Francisco_Guerrero%28001%29.JPG/440px-Asesinato_de_Francisco_Guerrero%28001%29.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Asesinato_de_Francisco_Guerrero(001).JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The image shown is by the Mexican artist, <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Guadalupe_Posada" title="José Guadalupe Posada">José Guadalupe Posada</a>. It shows a serial killer named <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Guerrero_(killer)" title="Francisco Guerrero (killer)">Francisco Guerrero</a>, or "The Mexican Ripper".</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Collecting art created by convicted serial killers has become a special pastime for some. <a href="/wiki/John_Wayne_Gacy" title="John Wayne Gacy">John Wayne Gacy</a> drew and painted art from prison, much of which he gave away. Some people took Gacy's work just to trash or burn it, especially after discovering that many of his images depicted his own victims.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Books">Books</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Serial_killer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Books">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>There is a huge market for "<a href="/wiki/True_crime" title="True crime">true crime</a>" and mystery murder novels;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup> some of the more successful authors are <a href="/wiki/Truman_Capote" title="Truman Capote">Truman Capote</a>, <a href="/wiki/Philip_Carlo" title="Philip Carlo">Philip Carlo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Patricia_Cornwell" title="Patricia Cornwell">Patricia Cornwell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Max_Haines" title="Max Haines">Max Haines</a>, <a href="/wiki/James_Patterson" title="James Patterson">James Patterson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ann_Rule" title="Ann Rule">Ann Rule</a>, <a href="/wiki/Harold_Schechter" title="Harold Schechter">Harold Schechter</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Peter_Vronsky" title="Peter Vronsky">Peter Vronsky</a>. <a href="/wiki/Robert_Louis_Stevenson" title="Robert Louis Stevenson">Robert Louis Stevenson</a>'s novella, <i><a href="/wiki/Strange_Case_of_Dr_Jekyll_and_Mr_Hyde" title="Strange Case of Dr Jekyll and Mr Hyde">Strange Case of Dr Jekyll and Mr Hyde</a></i> (1886), can be seen as a metaphor for the complex personality of the organized serial killer type that later disintegrates into the disorganized version. One of the greatest themes of this book, however, is the possibility that the dualistic conflict seen in Jekyll/Hyde could happen to anyone.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tod_Robbins" title="Tod Robbins">Tod Robbins</a>' novel <i>Mysterious Martin</i> (1912) is an early example of a horror novel focused on a serial killer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Dorothy_B._Hughes" title="Dorothy B. Hughes">Dorothy B. Hughes</a>' novel <i><a href="/wiki/In_a_Lonely_Place_(novel)" title="In a Lonely Place (novel)">In a Lonely Place</a></i> (1947) offers a striking, insightful portrait of a serial killer post <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/WWII" title="WWII">WWII</a>. Other notable literature with a serial killer theme includes <a href="/wiki/Bret_Easton_Ellis" title="Bret Easton Ellis">Bret Easton Ellis</a>' <i><a href="/wiki/American_Psycho" title="American Psycho">American Psycho</a></i> (1991), <a href="/wiki/Davis_Grubb" title="Davis Grubb">Davis Grubb</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/The_Night_of_the_Hunter_(novel)" title="The Night of the Hunter (novel)">The Night of the Hunter</a></i> (1955), <a href="/wiki/Jim_Thompson_(writer)" title="Jim Thompson (writer)">Jim Thompson</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/The_Killer_Inside_Me" title="The Killer Inside Me">The Killer Inside Me</a></i> (1952), and <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Harris" title="Thomas Harris">Thomas Harris</a>' books, <i><a href="/wiki/Red_Dragon_(novel)" title="Red Dragon (novel)">Red Dragon</a></i> (1981), <i><a href="/wiki/The_Silence_of_the_Lambs_(novel)" title="The Silence of the Lambs (novel)">The Silence of the Lambs</a></i> (1988), <i><a href="/wiki/Hannibal_(Harris_novel)" title="Hannibal (Harris novel)">Hannibal</a></i> (1999), and <i><a href="/wiki/Hannibal_Rising" title="Hannibal Rising">Hannibal Rising</a></i> (2006), all featuring <a href="/wiki/Hannibal_Lecter" title="Hannibal Lecter">Hannibal Lecter</a>, a brilliant <a href="/wiki/Psychiatrist" title="Psychiatrist">psychiatrist</a> who is also a <a href="/wiki/Cannibalism" title="Cannibalism">cannibalistic</a> serial killer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENewitz200623.E2.80.9337_160-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENewitz200623.E2.80.9337-160">[160]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESeltzer1998156_161-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESeltzer1998156-161">[161]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Film">Film</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Serial_killer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Film">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The already vast and continually growing production of serial killer-based works shows that the serial killer persona fascinates portions of western culture.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> For example, one of <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Edison" title="Thomas Edison">Thomas Edison</a>'s first <a href="/wiki/Phonograph" title="Phonograph">phonograph</a> recordings dealt with the confessions of serial killer <a href="/wiki/H._H._Holmes" title="H. H. Holmes">H. H. Holmes</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchmid2007.5B.5BCategory:Wikipedia_articles_needing_page_number_citations_from_February_2011.5D.5D.3Csup_class.3D.22noprint_Inline-Template_.22_style.3D.22white-space:nowrap.3B.22.3E.5B.3Ci.3E.5B.5BWikipedia:Citing_sources.7C.3Cspan_title.3D.22This_citation_requires_a_reference_to_the_specific_page_or_range_of_pages_in_which_the_material_appears..7F.27.22.60UNIQ--nowiki-000000FE-QINU.60.22.27.7F_.28February_2011.29.22.3Epage.C2.A0needed.3C.2Fspan.3E.5D.5D.3C.2Fi.3E.5D.3C.2Fsup.3E_162-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchmid2007.5B.5BCategory:Wikipedia_articles_needing_page_number_citations_from_February_2011.5D.5D.3Csup_class.3D.22noprint_Inline-Template_.22_style.3D.22white-space:nowrap.3B.22.3E.5B.3Ci.3E.5B.5BWikipedia:Citing_sources.7C.3Cspan_title.3D.22This_citation_requires_a_reference_to_the_specific_page_or_range_of_pages_in_which_the_material_appears..7F.27.22.60UNIQ--nowiki-000000FE-QINU.60.22.27.7F_.28February_2011.29.22.3Epage.C2.A0needed.3C.2Fspan.3E.5D.5D.3C.2Fi.3E.5D.3C.2Fsup.3E-162">[162]</a></sup> The creation of a monster helps society cope with the darker side of humanity but may lead to desensitization of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Media_violence" title="Media violence">media violence</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup></p>
<p>Serial killers are featured as <a href="/wiki/Stock_character" title="Stock character">stock characters</a> in many types of media, not only in films, but in including printed works, songs, television programs, and video games as well.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERoy200290_164-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERoy200290-164">[164]</a></sup> Films featuring serial killers include <i><a href="/wiki/The_Terror_(1928_film)" title="The Terror (1928 film)">The Terror</a></i> (1928), <i><a href="/wiki/M_(1931_film)" title="M (1931 film)">M</a></i> (1931), <i><a href="/wiki/Psycho_(1960_film)" title="Psycho (1960 film)">Psycho</a></i> (1960), <i><a href="/wiki/Henry:_Portrait_of_a_Serial_Killer" title="Henry: Portrait of a Serial Killer">Henry: Portrait of a Serial Killer</a></i> (1986), <i><a href="/wiki/The_Silence_of_the_Lambs_(film)" title="The Silence of the Lambs (film)">The Silence of the Lambs</a></i> (1991), <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Peeping_Tom" title="Peeping Tom">Peeping Tom</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Texas_Chain_Saw_Massacre" title="The Texas Chain Saw Massacre">The Texas Chain Saw Massacre</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Watcher_(film)" title="The Watcher (film)">The Watcher</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Mr._Brooks" title="Mr. Brooks">Mr. Brooks</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Dirty_Harry" title="Dirty Harry">Dirty Harry</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Zodiac_(film)" title="Zodiac (film)">Zodiac</a></i> (2007), <i><a href="/wiki/Seven_(1995_film)" title="Seven (1995 film)">Seven</a></i>, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Beachcomber" title="The Beachcomber">The Beachcomber</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Copycat_(film)" title="Copycat (film)">Copycat</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Halloween_(1978_film)" title="Halloween (1978 film)">Halloween</a></i> (1978), <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scream_(film_series)" title="Scream (film series)">Scream</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Frailty_(film)" title="Frailty (film)">Frailty</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Man_Bites_Dog_(film)" title="Man Bites Dog (film)">Man Bites Dog</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hitcher_(1986_film)" title="The Hitcher (1986 film)">The Hitcher</a></i> (1986), <i><a href="/wiki/Monster_(2003_film)" title="Monster (2003 film)">Monster</a></i> (2003), <i><a href="/wiki/Kalifornia" title="Kalifornia">Kalifornia</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Felidae_(film)" title="Felidae (film)">Felidae</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Killer_Inside_Me_(2010_film)" title="The Killer Inside Me (2010 film)">The Killer Inside Me</a></i> (2010), <i><a href="/wiki/Child%27s_Play_(1988_film)" title="Child's Play (1988 film)">Child's Play</a></i>, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Plastic_(2012_film)" title="Plastic (2012 film)">Plastic</a></i>, and many others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERoy200290_164-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERoy200290-164">[164]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchmid2005112-115_165-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchmid2005112-115-165">[165]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Memorabilia">Memorabilia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Serial_killer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Memorabilia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Notorious and infamous serial killers number in the hundreds, and a subculture revolves around their legacies. That subculture includes the collection, sale, and display of serial killer memorabilia, dubbed "<a href="/wiki/Murderabilia" title="Murderabilia">murderabilia</a>" by one of the best-known opponents of collectors of serial killer remnants, Andrew Kahan. He is the director of the Mayor's Crime Victims Office in Houston and is backed by the families of murder victims and "<a href="/wiki/Son_of_Sam_law" title="Son of Sam law">Son of Sam laws</a>" existing in some states that prevent murderers from profiting from the publicity generated by their crimes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ramsland_166-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ramsland-166">[166]</a></sup></p>
<p>Murderabilia includes the paintings, writings, and poems of these killers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup> Recently, marketing has capitalized even more upon interest in serial killers with the rise of various merchandise such as <a href="/wiki/Trading_card" title="Trading card">trading cards</a>, <a href="/wiki/Action_figure" title="Action figure">action figures</a>, and books such as <i>The Serial Killer Files: The Who, What, Where, How, and Why of the World's Most Terrifying Murderers</i> by <a href="/wiki/Harold_Schechter" title="Harold Schechter">Harold Schechter</a>, and <i>The A-Z Encyclopedia of Serial Killers</i> by Schecter and David Everitt. Some serial killers literally attain celebrity status in the way they acquire fans, and may have previous personal possessions auctioned off on websites like <a href="/wiki/EBay" title="EBay">eBay</a>. A few examples of this are <a href="/wiki/Ed_Gein" title="Ed Gein">Ed Gein</a>'s 150-pound stolen gravestone and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bobbie_Joe_Long" title="Bobbie Joe Long">Bobbie Joe Long</a>'s sunglasses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Serial_killer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_songs_about_killers" title="List of songs about killers">List of songs about killers</a></div>
<p>Modern singers and bands, some more popular than others, have felt the fascination and horror toward certain celebrity serial killers, writing their own songs about them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup> The Chicago-based metal band <a href="/wiki/Macabre_(band)" title="Macabre (band)">Macabre</a> boasts an entire back-catalogue of songs about serial killers, and even refer to their own particular style of music as <i><a href="/wiki/Murder_Metal" title="Murder Metal">Murder Metal</a></i>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Television">Television</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Serial_killer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Television">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>The CBS television show <i><a href="/wiki/Criminal_Minds" title="Criminal Minds">Criminal Minds</a></i> follows the cases of an FBI <a href="/wiki/Behavioral_Analysis_Unit" title="Behavioral Analysis Unit">Behavioral Analysis Unit</a> as it pursues serial killers and <a href="/wiki/Mass_murder" title="Mass murder">mass murderers</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup></li>
<li>The Showtime television series <i><a href="/wiki/Dexter_(TV_series)" title="Dexter (TV series)">Dexter</a></i> revolves around <a href="/wiki/Dexter_Morgan" title="Dexter Morgan">Dexter Morgan</a>, a police <a href="/wiki/Bloodstain_pattern_analysis" title="Bloodstain pattern analysis">blood-spatter pattern analyst</a> who moonlights as a vigilante serial killer attempting to channel his homicidal urges in a "positive" direction, by killing other murderers who have slipped through the cracks of the legal system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup> It is based on the novel <i><a href="/wiki/Darkly_Dreaming_Dexter" title="Darkly Dreaming Dexter">Darkly Dreaming Dexter</a></i> and features multiple serial killers over the life of the show.</li>
<li>The NBC television series <i><a href="/wiki/Hannibal_(TV_series)" title="Hannibal (TV series)">Hannibal</a></i> is based on characters and elements appearing in Thomas Harris' novel <i>Red Dragon</i> (1981), and focuses on the relationship between FBI special investigator Will Graham (Hugh Dancy) and Dr. Hannibal Lecter (Mads Mikkelsen), a forensic psychiatrist and serial killer destined to become Graham's most cunning enemy.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Netflix" title="Netflix">Netflix Original</a> series, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Fall_(TV_series)" title="The Fall (TV series)">The Fall</a></i>, follows the activities of serial killer Paul Peter Spector, aka Peter Baldwin, the efforts of the Belfast police team, first assisted then headed by Stella Gibson, to catch him, and the effects of both sides' activities on others.</li>
<li>Season 3 of the AMC television series <i><a href="/wiki/The_Killing_(U.S._TV_series)" title="The Killing (U.S. TV series)">The Killing</a></i> (2013) focuses largely on identifying and capturing a Seattle-area serial killer of prostitutes and street kids, who may also have killed the wife of an inmate sentenced to death for her murder.</li>
<li>The CBS television series <i><a href="/wiki/The_Mentalist" title="The Mentalist">The Mentalist</a></i> has as its central antagonist a serial killer known as <a href="/wiki/Red_John" title="Red John">Red John</a>, who until the end of season 5 has murdered about 28 people, including the protagonist's wife and daughter, the <a href="/wiki/California_Bureau_of_Investigation" title="California Bureau of Investigation">CBI</a> consultant <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Jane" title="Patrick Jane">Patrick Jane</a>. Discovering Red John's identity and avenging his victims' deaths are Jane and the series' main goals.</li>
<li>Season 1 of the <a href="/wiki/HBO" title="HBO">HBO</a> series <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/True_Detective_(TV_series)" title="True Detective (TV series)">True Detective</a></i> follows two detectives who are investigating a mysterious serial killer known as the Yellow King.</li>
<li>The ABC procedural drama television series <i><a href="/wiki/Wicked_City_(TV_series)" title="Wicked City (TV series)">Wicked City</a></i> (October 27, 2015 to December 30, 2015) focuses on two <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/LAPD" title="LAPD">LAPD</a> detectives (Jeremy Sisto and Gabriel Luna) as they search for a pair of romantically-linked serial killers (Ed Westwick and Erika Christensen) terrorizing the <a href="/wiki/Sunset_Strip" title="Sunset Strip">Sunset Strip</a>.</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Toys">Toys</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Serial_killer&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Toys">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Spectre_Studios" title="Spectre Studios">Spectre Studios</a> was a Colorado toy company making action figures of serial killers including <a href="/wiki/Lizzie_Borden" title="Lizzie Borden">Lizzie Borden</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ted_Bundy" title="Ted Bundy">Ted Bundy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jeffrey_Dahmer" title="Jeffrey Dahmer">Jeffrey Dahmer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ed_Gein" title="Ed Gein">Ed Gein</a>, <a href="/wiki/Charles_Manson" title="Charles Manson">Charles Manson</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pogo_the_Clown" title="Pogo the Clown">Pogo the Clown</a>.</li>
</ul>

Barri Flowers (2012). <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=MQnSBQAAQBAJ&amp;pg=PA195" rel="nofollow"><i>The Dynamics of Murder: Kill or Be Killed</i></a>. <a href="/wiki/CRC_Press" title="CRC Press">CRC Press</a>. p. 195. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/1439879745" title="Special:BookSources/1439879745">1439879745</a><span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">June 15,</span> 2016</span>. <q>In general, most experts on serial murder require that a minimum of three murders be committed at different times and usually different places for a person to qualify as a serial killer.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASerial+killer&amp;rft.au=R.+Barri+Flowers&amp;rft.btitle=The+Dynamics+of+Murder%3A+Kill+or+Be+Killed&amp;rft.date=2012&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DMQnSBQAAQBAJ%26pg%3DPA195&amp;rft.isbn=1439879745&amp;rft.pages=195&amp;rft.pub=CRC+Press&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></li>
<li><cite class="citation book">Harold Schechter (2012). <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=zM7ROzJPK2MC&amp;pg=PA73" rel="nofollow"><i>The A to Z Encyclopedia of Serial Killers</i></a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Simon_and_Schuster" title="Simon and Schuster">Simon and Schuster</a>. p. 73. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/1439138850" title="Special:BookSources/1439138850">1439138850</a><span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">June 15,</span> 2016</span>. <q>Most experts seem to agree, however, that to qualify as a serial killer, an individual has to slay a minimum of three unrelated victims.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASerial+killer&amp;rft.au=Harold+Schechter&amp;rft.btitle=The+A+to+Z+Encyclopedia+of+Serial+Killers&amp;rft.date=2012&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DzM7ROzJPK2MC%26pg%3DPA73&amp;rft.isbn=1439138850&amp;rft.pages=73&amp;rft.pub=Simon+and+Schuster&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></li>

<li id="cite_note-Hough-3"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Hough_3-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Hough_3-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Richard M.
